Ultimate website of large numbers (illions version)

This website is made by Bella Tersumi. We're all familiar with numbers like million, billion, or trillion - but how far do the "illion" numbers go, the furthest Bowers has seen in the literature is milli-millillion (10^3000003) which he calls a micrillion. Some time ago (about 15 years or so), being interested in giant numbers, Bowers have invented names for illion numbers past a centillion (highest that he has seen in books at that time) - by continuing the trend: deci, centi, by using milli, micro, nano, pico, femto, and atto. Sometime later, Bowers found out that he wasn't the only one to choose the name "millillion" for 10^3003 - Bowers found this name mentioned on Robert Munafo's fascinating web site on large numbers. Following is a list of the "illion" numbers (those above millillion are names he invented), along with googol, googolplex, and googolduplex for size reference. The ones less than micrillion are shown on the above mentioned web site, naming rules up to the millillion range are mentioned in The Book of Numbers by Conway and Guy. Bowers recently changed some of the numbers to match with the polytope suffixes. As of November 15th 2022, due to the new prefixes ronna, ronto, quetta, and quecto, I changed a few illion names. I renamed all of CompactStar's illion names due to confusion comparing metillion and betillion having two possible names. As of December 2024, Hisham Shakeel decides to add brunta, bramto, agana, and azeko to the Metric Prefix, thanks to him for the idea.
